 succeeded in 0ms:
   500	**Watch for:** the spawned manifest task holds a clone of `tx`. The
   501	original `tx` is dropped explicitly after the response loop. Daemon
   502	sees end-of-stream only when *all* clones drop. Verify the sequence
   503	makes the daemon see EOF reliably (it does in current testing, but
   504	the ordering is subtle).
   505	
   506	### 7.5 push small-file completion race (`60d152f`, `5bb78d9`)
   507	
   508	The push client's early `data_plane_sender.finish()` could fire while
   509	the daemon was still sending need-list batches (because
   510	`files_requested` only reflected need-lists *already received*). Closing
   511	the data plane mid-stream caused the daemon's `upload_tx` receiver to
   512	drop, and subsequent manifest entries failed to enqueue.
   513	
   514	Fix: daemon now always emits an empty `FilesToUpload` as a "no more
   515	need-lists" terminator; client sets `need_lists_done = true` on
   516	receipt and gates the early finish on that flag. 9% completion → 100%
   517	completion verified.
   518	
   519	```rust
   520	// daemon side: FileListBatcher::finish always flushes terminator
   521	async fn finish(mut self) -> Result<(), Status> {
   522	    if !self.batch.is_empty() { self.flush().await?; }
   523	    // Always emit empty terminator — discrete "no more need_lists" signal.
   524	    send_control_message(&self.tx,
   525	        server_push_response::Payload::FilesToUpload(FileList { relative_paths: Vec::new() })
   526	    ).await?;
   527	    Ok(())
   528	}
   529	
   530	// client side: gate early finish
   531	if matches!(transfer_mode, TransferMode::DataPlane)
   532	    && !need_list_fresh
   533	    && need_lists_done   // <-- new
   534	    && pending_queue.is_empty()
   535	    && manifest_done
   536	    && data_plane_outstanding == 0
   537	    && data_plane_files_sent >= files_requested.len()
   538	{
   539	    if let Some(sender) = data_plane_sender.take() { sender.finish().await?; }
   540	}
   541	```
   542	
   543	**Watch for:** old daemon × new client interactions. The daemon now
   544	emits a trailing empty FilesToUpload that an old client would
   545	interpret as a 0-entry need-list (harmless — it advances the loop
   546	once more). New daemon × old client never receives the terminator and
   547	falls back to the post-loop `finish()` after `Summary` arrives.
   548	
   549	### 7.6 Daemon push-receive backpressure (`b64bfd8`)
   550	
   551	The control plane's gRPC loop pushes manifest entries into an mpsc
   552	that the data plane previously consumed. After the receive
   553	unification (which gets metadata off the wire instead of from the
   554	cache), the consumer is gone — but the producer would still block on
   555	`upload_tx.send().await` if no one drained.

- **High — `docs/plan/UNIFIED_TRANSFER_ENGINE_REV4.md` / Acceptance Criteria, Design §5, Risks, Revised Slices.** REV4 still requires mixed-version behavior, old/new peer compatibility tests, old peers seeing current behavior, and peer capability bits (`lines 146-166`, `357-365`, `406-410`, `439-442`, `460-474`). These are active requirements, not struck history, and directly contradict D-2026-07-05-2.

- **High — `proto/blit.proto` / wire comments.** Proto comments still define mixed-version fallback behavior and capability-advertisement semantics for `DataTransferNegotiation`, `TransferOperationSpec`, and `PeerCapabilities` (`lines 138-176`, `587-624`, `665-688`, `772-790`). This also contaminates the receiver-capacity carve-out by describing it as old-peer fallback instead of hardware-only negotiation.

- **Medium — `docs/WHITEPAPER.md` / §7.5 push small-file completion race.** Current reviewer guidance still asks readers to watch old-daemon/new-client and new-daemon/old-client interactions (`lines 543-547`). That leaves a live doc implying mixed-build compatibility remains a review concern.

VERDICT: NEEDS FIXES — D-2026-07-05-2 and ONE_TRANSFER_PATH otp-1 are concrete enough at the plan level, but active REV4/proto/whitepaper text still preserves forbidden compatibility work.
